## Section 001: Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed no seed line states what this theme actually spans, two whole skill-creation systems from the same month, the Claude plugin bundle whose 479-line entrypoint plus three agent prompts and a schema sheet build a quantitative evaluation harness, and the Codex system skill whose 416 lines teach principles-first authoring with forward-testing, plus a live-tree copy of the Claude bundle verified byte-identical to its archive
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because both platforms shipped a skill for making skills in 202603, and each encoded its platform's evaluation philosophy, Claude measuring skills with baselines, assertions, and benchmark deltas, Codex stress-testing them through uncontaminated subagent runs, so the theme's real subject is how skill quality gets proven, not just how skills get written
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: reading the bundle as one doctrine merges two incompatible evaluation designs, a benchmark harness that needs baseline runs and exact JSON schemas, and a forward-testing discipline that forbids leaking context to the tester, advice from one misapplied under the other breaks both
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference covers the two creator systems and their evaluation methods, the skills they create are governed by their own themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the two-system inventory, the identical live copy, and the evaluation-philosophy split as the organizing contrast
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Skill Creator Evaluation Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the live claude-skills tree carrying a byte-identical copy of the archived plugin means the archive is not merely historical here, it is a verified snapshot of the working tool, the only theme so far whose ancestor evidence and current deployment are provably the same bytes, collapsing the archive-versus-live caveat that every other theme must carry

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 006: External Research Source Map
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed three inherited agent-format anchors stand while the theme's real external surface is the platform machinery its workflows invoke, the claude CLI that trigger optimization shells out to, the subagent task notifications whose total_tokens and duration_ms fields the timing capture depends on, and the Codex-side init_skill.py and quick_validate.py scripts whose flags the guide freezes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because both systems couple to their platforms at documented seams, and those seams are volatile, a notification payload change silently breaks timing capture, a CLI flag change breaks run_loop.py, so the external map should watch platform interfaces, not generic format sites
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: trusting the frozen seam documentation on a current platform risks exactly the timing-capture failure the hub warns is unrecoverable, the data comes through the notification and isn't persisted elsewhere

- **revision_decision:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the inherited rows, add the load-bearing seams, platform subagent notification schemas and the claude CLI's programmatic interface, and mark all seam descriptions archive-dated

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the harness expresses its quality doctrine as commands the way the Rust family expresses its as cargo gates, each command freezes a workflow stage, aggregation, presentation, optimization, validation, into a reproducible invocation

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed four generic bullets stand where the systems define a five-role agent cast, the orchestrating creator who runs the loop, executor subagents who run test prompts with or without the skill, the grader who scores assertions with evidence, the blind comparator who judges unattributed outputs, and the analyzer who unblinds and explains, each role with its own prompt document and information boundary
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the roles exist to partition knowledge, executors must not know they are being tested, the comparator must not know which skill made which output, the grader must not accept claims without evidence, so the cast is an information architecture, not a task decomposition
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: collapsing roles collapses boundaries, an orchestrator who grades its own runs knows what it hoped to see, the exact bias the grader's burden-of-proof rule and the comparator's blindness exist to exclude
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: agent roles inside the evaluation harness, the created skills' own agent usage belongs to their themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recast the section as the five-role cast with each role's knowledge boundary and prompt document
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the Codex guide runs the same partition with two roles instead of five, author and uncontaminated forward-tester, showing the knowledge-partition principle scales down, what cannot scale down is zero roles, the author alone, both systems treat single-agent self-evaluation as the failure state their whole architecture exists to prevent

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed one generic engineer stands where the Claude entrypoint itself maps the journeys, the from-scratch creator whom the skill walks from intent capture through iteration, the improver who arrives with a draft and jumps straight to the eval loop, the vibe collaborator who declines rigor and gets flexibility by name, and the plumber, the entrypoint's own image of newly-empowered non-programmers who need jargon translated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's opening section instructs the agent to locate the user in the process and join there, so journey identification is not analysis overlaid on the source, it is the source's own first instruction
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: ignoring the journey step produces the misfit the guide warns about, walking a draft-holding improver through intent-capture interviews, or drowning the plumber in assertion JSON the communication section says to translate

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed template rows skip the systems' live tensions, rigor versus velocity, the full benchmark loop versus the sanctioned vibe path, freedom versus constraint in the Codex degrees-of-freedom ladder, narrow bridges get scripts, open fields get prose, and generalization versus responsiveness, fixing the user's specific complaint versus the fiddly-overfitty warning against changes that only serve known examples
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each axis is decided per-skill and per-user, both guides refuse global answers, the Claude guide bends rigor to user election, the Codex guide indexes freedom to task fragility, and both subordinate specific fixes to million-invocation generality
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: wrong poles fail characteristically, forced rigor alienates the vibe user, low-freedom scripts strangle tasks needing judgment, high-freedom prose lets fragile operations wobble, and complaint-chasing builds skills that only pass their own evals
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: tuning decisions inside the creator systems, created skills inherit the degrees-of-freedom analysis for their own content

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside the systems' own retry doctrine, the harness retries at iteration granularity, rerun all test cases into a fresh iteration directory after each improvement, never reuse stale runs, the forward-tester retries with fresh threads and cleaned artifacts to prevent cross-iteration contamination, and the Cowork adaptation sanctions series execution as backpressure when parallel subagents hit timeouts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because evaluation retries differ from network retries, the hazard is not transient failure but state leakage, stale eval metadata, prior-iteration artifacts a subagent can find, so both systems' retry rules are contamination rules wearing retry clothes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: reusing prior runs after a skill edit measures a mixture of versions, and leaving artifacts on disk lets later forward-tests succeed by finding earlier answers, both producing confident numbers about nothing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry semantics inside skill evaluation, network-level retry doctrine belongs to the reliability themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the iteration-granularity rule, fresh directories, fresh metadata, fresh baselines per the create-versus-improve rule, and the contamination hygiene, fresh threads, cleaned artifacts, series fallback under timeout pressure
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the entrypoint's warning that eval metadata does not carry over between iterations is a cache-invalidation rule for evidence, every iteration's evidence must be regenerated from the current skill version, evaluation state is never warm-startable, the one place where recomputing from scratch is the correctness requirement rather than the naive baseline
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to regenerate everything per iteration, clean the workspace of findable answers, and drop to series execution when the platform pushes back
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because evaluation retries differ from network retries, the hazard is not transient failure but state leakage, stale eval metadata, prior-iteration artifacts a subagent can find, so both systems' retry rules are contamination rules wearing retry clothes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; reusing prior runs after a skill edit measures a mixture of versions, and leaving artifacts on disk lets later forward-tests succeed by finding earlier answers, both producing confident numbers about nothing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: retry semantics inside skill evaluation, network-level retry doctrine belongs to the reliability themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: state the iteration-granularity rule, fresh directories, fresh metadata, fresh baselines per the create-versus-improve rule, and the contamination hygiene, fresh threads, cleaned artifacts, series fallback under timeout pressure
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the entrypoint's warning that eval metadata does not carry over between iterations is a cache-invalidation rule for evidence, every iteration's evidence must be regenerated from the current skill version, evaluation state is never warm-startable, the one place where recomputing from scratch is the correctness requirement rather than the naive baseline

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic records stand beside the harness's observability design, which is unusually complete, transcripts persisted per run, timing captured at the notification moment or lost, metrics JSON counting tool calls and errors, grading evidence quoting its sources, analyst notes surfacing what aggregates hide, and user notes flagging executor uncertainties upward into grading
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the harness treats every run as an evidence-producing event whose observability is designed in advance, because its whole epistemology depends on being able to show why a number is what it is
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: each missing record breaks a documented consumer, no transcript starves the analyzer's execution-pattern reading, no timing empties the benchmark's resource columns irrecoverably, no evidence field turns grades into assertions about assertions
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the harness's run-level records plus this node's own evidence records, established in the completeness and metrics sections
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt the harness's record inventory as the section's core, transcripts, timing, metrics, evidenced grades, analyst notes, user notes, each with its documented consumer named
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the user-notes channel is the harness's most humane record, executors flag their own uncertainties and workarounds, and the grader is instructed to read them because they may reveal problems even when expectations pass, a designed path for the executing agent's doubt to survive into the quality verdict, doubt as a first-class observable

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside the systems' own scale limits, the harness scales to a handful of evals iterated by one attentive user, its viewer, feedback loop, and same-turn spawn design all assume single-digit test cases, and the entrypoint says so, expand the test set and try again at larger scale is the exit, not the loop, while the Codex guide bounds SKILL.md at 500 lines and pushes overflow into referenced files
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the human review loop is the harness's throughput ceiling, one user clicking through outputs caps eval count long before compute does, and context economics cap skill length, both systems name their own boundaries explicitly
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: past the eval ceiling, feedback quality collapses before run capacity does, users skim instead of review, and past the line ceiling, skills hog the context window the Codex guide calls a public good
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: bounding the creator systems' designed operating ranges, created skills' own scale limits belong to their content
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name both limits with their documented exits, larger-scale test expansion after loop convergence, and progressive-disclosure splitting at the line boundary
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that both boundaries are attention budgets, the eval ceiling rations the user's reviewing attention, the line ceiling rations the model's context attention, and both systems solve them the same way, progressive disclosure, the harness discloses outputs one test case at a time in the viewer exactly as skills disclose content one reference file at a time, one design principle governing both the tool and its products
